  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8e61b2ad-dfb8-4769-a8f6-9116d2517c6a'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1214940808" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1214940808" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1214940808?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780312106089" href="/book/show/1487805.Brotherhood_of_the_Rose">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=spies">spies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1214940808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15861256656438342662"><b>”In Greek mythology, the god of love once offered a rose to the god of silence, as a bribe, to keep that god from disclosing the weaknesses of the other gods. In time, the rose became the symbol for silence and secrecy. In the Middle ages, a rose was customarily suspended from the ceiling of a council chamber. The members of the council pledged themselves not to reveal what they discussed in the room, <i>sub rosa</i> under the rose.”</b><br/><br/>There once were two boys named Romulus and Remus, not the two founders</span>
  <span id="freeText15861256656438342662" style="display:none"><b>”In Greek mythology, the god of love once offered a rose to the god of silence, as a bribe, to keep that god from disclosing the weaknesses of the other gods. In time, the rose became the symbol for silence and secrecy. In the Middle ages, a rose was customarily suspended from the ceiling of a council chamber. The members of the council pledged themselves not to reveal what they discussed in the room, <i>sub rosa</i> under the rose.”</b><br /><br />There once were two boys named Romulus and Remus, not the two founders of Rome, but two boys who found each other in an orphanage in Pennsylvania. They became closer than brothers. Isn’t that the case with many of us, finding our close friends to be more our brothers and sisters than our own flesh and blood? Chris (Remus) is visited periodically by a gray faced man named Eliot who starts every visit by extending a Baby Ruth candy bar. In an orphanage you are more likely to find a bar of gold than a bar of chocolate. He takes Chris on backpacking trips and fishing trips. Soon Saul (Romulus) joins them. As they grow up their foster father suggests certain activities for them such as Karate. When they are old enough he suggests they join the military. They are sent to Vietnam. <br /><br />Suggestions from Eliot are the same as commands. <br /><br />They don’t know it until later, but Eliot has several pairs of orphaned boys from various cities. Castor and Pollux, Cadmus and Cilix, Amphion and Zethus, Butes and Erectheus, and Atlas and Prometheus. They are all trained to be operatives for a shadowy sector of the CIA. The reverence they all show for Eliot borders on worship. <br /><br />Eliot is also part of a national coalition of spies that formed a system called the Abelard Sanctuary. <i>"I had come there as a fugitive and, in the depths of my despair, was granted some comfort by the grace of God.”</i> Peter Abélard (1079-1142) was a brilliant rising star of theology, philosophy, and logician who fell in love with the scholar of classical letters Héloïse. They are secretly married to appease her uncle, but when he announces the marriage publicly it is denied by the couple. The Uncle is sure that Abélard is up to no good so he hires some thugs to pay him a visit. <br /><br />They castrate him. <br /><br />The letters of longing between Abélard and Héloïse become some of the most famous love letters of all time and forever immortalized the couple among the most legendary of doomed lovers rivaled only by Shakespeare’s creation of Romeo and Juliet. Abélard becomes a monk, but has difficulties with the monastery system and eventually retires to a chapel at Paraclete. He went there seeking sanctuary. If he wished to remain anonymous or forgotten it did not work. Students appeared living in tents around the chapel and soon he is teaching once again. <br /><br />The coalition of spies from all over the world find that there are times when they need sanctuary. They reach an agreement to place these Abelard Sanctuaries strategically all over the world. For those that have seen the recent movie <i>John Wick</i>, starring Keanu Reeves, the hotel in the movie is based on the same concept as an Abelard Sanctuary. No one is allowed to kill within the walls of sanctuary. If someone breaks the truce all of the nations participating are forced by the rules of the contract to do their best to execute the killer. It is a place where enemies can mingle without fear. <br /><br />Everything is going fine until Saul is ordered to blow up a close friend of the President of the United States. The assassination was made to look like the Israelis for political reasons. When Saul goes to his designated safe house some men are there to try to kill him. <br /><br />He has been blacklisted. <br /><br />His first thought is to call his foster father, but that was the source of the safe house location. Is it possible that the person he revers most in the world could be wanting to kill him? <br /><br />Saul is forced on the run for his life. He meets up with Chris and between the two of them they come up with a plan of survival. Betrayals begat betrayals and soon all that they think they believe in is suddenly nothing more than an enigma of deception. To survive they will have to embrace revenge. <br /><br />The pacing of the novel is excellent. It is certainly a page turner. David Morrell is an old hand at deftly keeping the plot from faltering. The secrecy attributed to the rose becomes an obsession for many of the Abelard Sanctuary group. Many of them begin cultivating them as a hobby, all becoming as bewitched by their beauty as the Dutch were about tulips in the 17th century. Some reviewers have found the sanctuary concept, a truce between foes, to be verging on science fiction, but for me it makes sense. The men and women who work behind the cloak of secrecy have much more in common with each other than they do with the countries they call home. By the definition of their careers they are lonely people, cut off from their families and friends, and reluctant to form relationships that could in the end compromise them. Sometimes your enemy knows you best and with them there are no pretenses about the job. <br /><br />My favorite David Morrell so far is: Murder As a Fine Art a book about Thomas De Quincey the famous British Opium Eater. The second book with De Quincey is scheduled to release in March. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/648484443?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Murder as a Fine Art Review</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15861256656438342662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_73376937" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/73376937" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/73376937?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780449206614" href="/book/show/922051.The_Brotherhood_of_the_Rose">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=spy-fi">spy-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73376937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5998381868293403434">One of my favorite writers from a few years ago. David Morrell is (was?) the king of conspiracies (from "a few years ago"). This is the poster child...two orphans raised from a very early age to be part of a group of ultra loyal assassins.<br/><br/>This one stayed with me and it's the one that sent me off finding other books by the author. The characters in this book are very well drawn (one more so than the other I believe) and will create in you a strange sympathy (for the boys...all the boys).<br/><br/>There was</span>
  <span id="freeText5998381868293403434" style="display:none">One of my favorite writers from a few years ago. David Morrell is (was?) the king of conspiracies (from "a few years ago"). This is the poster child...two orphans raised from a very early age to be part of a group of ultra loyal assassins.<br /><br />This one stayed with me and it's the one that sent me off finding other books by the author. The characters in this book are very well drawn (one more so than the other I believe) and will create in you a strange sympathy (for the boys...all the boys).<br /><br />There was also an acceptable movie/TV miniseries version of it done in 1989. It was (surprisingly) well done...but read the book.<br /><br />Another update. Every time I look back to an old review I find typos...<br /><br />But that said, I still recommend this book and find it one of my favorites by the author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5998381868293403434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_354270344" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/354270344" />
    <a title="Feliks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5085729-feliks"><img alt="Feliks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445015906p2/5085729.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/354270344?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Feliks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Feliks" href="/user/show/5085729-feliks">Feliks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5085729-feliks?shelf=genre-thrillers">genre-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer354270344" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1475518203340193007">So many commentators on the GR page for this book, seem to have absorbed the experience entirely wrong. Be in no doubt: <i>'Brotherhood of the Rose'</i> is is one of the greatest modern spy thrillers. I'll tell you precisely why, in a moment.<br/><br/>Just be aware first of all, that there was an interval in espionage publishing which had dragged on--just before this title appeared--in which nothing really excellent was being done. Nothing formidable had appeared for a while. Forsyth was quiet, Follett was quiet</span>
  <span id="freeText1475518203340193007" style="display:none">So many commentators on the GR page for this book, seem to have absorbed the experience entirely wrong. Be in no doubt: <i>'Brotherhood of the Rose'</i> is is one of the greatest modern spy thrillers. I'll tell you precisely why, in a moment.<br /><br />Just be aware first of all, that there was an interval in espionage publishing which had dragged on--just before this title appeared--in which nothing really excellent was being done. Nothing formidable had appeared for a while. Forsyth was quiet, Follett was quiet, LeCarre was quiet; Ludlum was static/predictable as always; and Alistair MacLean had jumped the shark...only Clive Cussler was around to (inadequately) supply the lack of gritty, tough, fast-moving, action-based reads. <br /><br />What does that say to you? It was a doldrum. If you look around now, yeah sure, with the friggin' internet and Amazon available to you...you have your choice of <i>thousands</i> of authors. All beating a path to your door. Do you think that is the <u>norm</u>? Its not. Plus, look at how 'copycat' all this new bounty is. You've got a glut of hacks angling for your attention now, but very few pioneers. Morrell was--is--a pioneer.<br /><br />This book emerged at the perfect moment for him to break through into the next level of his career. His very-solid writing skills were already established thanks to <i>'First Blood'</i> but there was really nothing quite like <em>'Brotherhood'</em> until he busted through the door with it. <i>'Rose'</i> essentially revived the action/spy genre; <b>all</b> commando fiction got-a-new-lease-on-life; got started-back-off-on-the-right-foot. He breathed life back into the body. Its a milestone work. Its the equal of--and successor to--iconic titles like 'Eiger Sanction', <u>'Marathon Man'</u>, and <u>'Odessa File'</u>.<br /><br />And here's why: the story doesn't rely on "whatever's going on in international politics" whenever you happen to pick it up and flip through it. The story is set in an <i>abstract world</i> of spies and assassins. Almost no specific agencies or countries are named. No real-world details or conditions are posed at the time of writing, which might later 'break' or become anachronistic. If you read it at the time-of-release--or read it today--its still just as good. A lot of the best thriller novels ever written, all possess this quality: they're based on scenarios which can <i>always work,</i> no matter the timeperiod.<br /><br />Its the same methodology William Goldman used with his invention of the hypothetical shadow-agency called <i>'the Division';</i> Forsyth explored with <i>'Die Spinne'</i> and which Trevanian employed with his mysterious <i>'C-II'</i> outfit. Saul and his brother (in this story) are 'on the run' from the <i>global espionage community;</i> they ricochet around the secret network of worldwide 'safe-houses' perennially relied on by that community. Thus, it has nothing to do with "what countries happen-to-be-playing-nice-with-each-other"...<i>lately.</i> <br /><br />"Today's friend is tomorrow's enemy", (as anyone in diplomacy knows). <i>'Brotherhood of the Rose'</i> works so well, because every decade of modern life holds spies, commandos, assassins, and espionage/counter-espionage agencies. They never go away; they are a fact of modern life. As long as there are nations; as long as the world has finite resources of metals and crops and timber and fisheries--spies and spy agencies will always be in motion behind the headlines. They will always be plausible in fiction; and for the authors (like David Morrell) who have the skill to craft stories about this sphere--they remain--as always--the great stand-bys of the action-genre.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1475518203340193007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Morrell likes his History which I appreciate.</span>

<div id="review_1262161302" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1262161302" />
    <a title="Pramod Nair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37107782-pramod-nair"><img alt="Pramod Nair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425650534p2/37107782.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1262161302?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pramod Nair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pramod Nair" href="/user/show/37107782-pramod-nair">Pramod Nair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37107782-pramod-nair?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37107782-pramod-nair?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37107782-pramod-nair?shelf=spy-thriller">spy-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1262161302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12779285882101412461">If you are a reader who loves taut, suspenseful spy thrillers from the cold war era with a good dose of plot twists and turns then you will definitely love ‘<b>The Brotherhood of the Rose</b>’. Written by ‘<i>David Morrell</i>’ - the man who created the legendary character ‘<i>John Rambo</i>’ - this classic espionage thriller, which is the first book in a trilogy, is full of spies, killers, trade-craft and high-octane action spread across locations all over the globe. <br/><br/>The author is a master in controlling the suspen</span>
  <span id="freeText12779285882101412461" style="display:none">If you are a reader who loves taut, suspenseful spy thrillers from the cold war era with a good dose of plot twists and turns then you will definitely love ‘<b>The Brotherhood of the Rose</b>’. Written by ‘<i>David Morrell</i>’ - the man who created the legendary character ‘<i>John Rambo</i>’ - this classic espionage thriller, which is the first book in a trilogy, is full of spies, killers, trade-craft and high-octane action spread across locations all over the globe. <br /><br />The author is a master in controlling the suspense factor so effectively that reading this book becomes a constant ‘<i>edge of the seat</i>’ affair. David Morrell’s characters are pretty strong and connect emotionally with the reader in a strong manner. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The plot revolves around two orphans <i>‘Chris’ &amp; ‘Saul’</i> - bonded like brothers - who are adopted by a mysterious man named Elliot, who treats them as his own children. ‘Chris’ &amp; ‘Saul’ are like blood brothers. He visited them at their orphanage and brought them chocolates and candy and taught them to love him as their father. Then over the course of their years growing up he trained them into perfect killing machines. After their service in army special forces they become expert operatives for a section of CIA controlled by Elliot. When Elliot finds both ‘Chris’ and ‘Saul’ expendable what follows is a pulse-pounding story of violent betrayal, intense loyalty and chilling revenge, which the reader will find a bit difficult to put down. It is the intensity that Morrell packs into the narration and Morrell’s eye for detailing which makes even the strangest suggestions and conspiracies from the author seems sensible for the reader. The core concept of the book about a brotherhood of spies from every intelligence community, which is entirely fictitious and invented by the author, seems realistic when Morrell narrates it through decades of CIA and other intelligence agencies history. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />‘The Brotherhood of the Rose’ is a book written purely for entertaining the reader and like other David Morrell Thrillers, it is <i>detailed, fast paced and pulsates with non-stop action</i> so that the fans of ‘<i>espionage thriller</i>’/ ‘<i>political thriller</i>’ genre will find it extremely satisfying. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12779285882101412461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1217969075" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1217969075" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/695116-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1217969075?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/695116-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780449206614" href="/book/show/922051.The_Brotherhood_of_the_Rose">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction">2fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=1paper">1paper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=3series">3series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1217969075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9651415952726484966">I'm really glad I reread this. It's been too long & I'd forgotten many of the details. Morrell does a great job spinning conspiracy theories together into an action packed, but quite believable adventure. If you like "The Black List" on TV (the 1st season) you'll love this book. I reread for Action/Adventure Aficionados group April 2016<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18069098'>https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/...</a><br/><br/>Morrell's writing is tight and the characters are well drawn. The conspiracies are deep, but easy to believe. Eliot is an </span>
  <span id="freeText9651415952726484966" style="display:none">I'm really glad I reread this. It's been too long &amp; I'd forgotten many of the details. Morrell does a great job spinning conspiracy theories together into an action packed, but quite believable adventure. If you like "The Black List" on TV (the 1st season) you'll love this book. I reread for Action/Adventure Aficionados group April 2016<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18069098">https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/...</a><br /><br />Morrell's writing is tight and the characters are well drawn. The conspiracies are deep, but easy to believe. Eliot is an old, powerful spymaster who has been the only good thing in the brutal life of Chris &amp; Saul who were orphaned early. He gave them kindness, attention, &amp; eventually purpose, but when needs must, the devil drives &amp; then there's hell to pay. Welcome to Hell where who did what to whom &amp; why becomes a question of survival, but who will survive? Who should?<br /><br />I've read several other books like this in the past year or so. Today authors jump the shark too often, but Morrell manages to create heroes &amp; heroines that don't need to go beyond the realm of reality to keep the action boiling. Very well done.<br /><br />----------------------<br />March 2005 Review:<br />It's been a long time since I read this, but a friend's review brought it to mind.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1214940808">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br />As I recall, it was very twisty &amp; quite good, but a little too full of angst for me. One or two other books of Morrell's tie in with this, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21837.The_Fraternity_Of_The_Stone__Mortalis___2_" title="The Fraternity Of The Stone (Mortalis, #2) by David Morrell" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fraternity Of The Stone</a> for sure. It's been a while since I read them &amp; it was years between, but I think it was just as good.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6402466657282056801">While initially getting into the book was hard to do, I really got attached to Chris and Saul, so much so that I found myself crying several times throughout the book. The characters of the brothers were well rounded and left you wondering how one could embrace violence so naturally and the other would later shy away from his life as an assassin. <br/><br/>I'm not sure why so many people brought up technology in their reviews, the book was written when people still knew what the phrase "cold war" meant. I</span>
  <span id="freeText6402466657282056801" style="display:none">While initially getting into the book was hard to do, I really got attached to Chris and Saul, so much so that I found myself crying several times throughout the book. The characters of the brothers were well rounded and left you wondering how one could embrace violence so naturally and the other would later shy away from his life as an assassin. <br /><br />I'm not sure why so many people brought up technology in their reviews, the book was written when people still knew what the phrase "cold war" meant. I didn't find that the "older" technology took anything from the book since the references were time appropriate. <br /><br />The ending could have been a little tighter in my opinion but ultimately it's a fascinating glimpse into the spy business as it was 20 years ago and the human connections that men in that business form. </span>

<div id="review_124919557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124919557" />
    <a title="Jeff" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/681671-jeff"><img alt="Jeff" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124919557?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeff" href="/user/show/681671-jeff">Jeff</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124919557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14092765132223608966">David Morrell, better known as the writer of the novel the first Rambo movie was based on, wrote a spy trilogy in the early 1980s that has just been released in ebook format.<br/>The first, Brotherhood of the Rose, follows two orphans that have been raised as brothers and trained to become expert operatives for a secret branch of the CIA.<br/>One of the things that sets this book apart from other spy novels is a great concept – on the eve of WWII all of the directors of the various intelligence organizati</span>
  <span id="freeText14092765132223608966" style="display:none">David Morrell, better known as the writer of the novel the first Rambo movie was based on, wrote a spy trilogy in the early 1980s that has just been released in ebook format.<br />The first, Brotherhood of the Rose, follows two orphans that have been raised as brothers and trained to become expert operatives for a secret branch of the CIA.<br />One of the things that sets this book apart from other spy novels is a great concept – on the eve of WWII all of the directors of the various intelligence organizations banded together to create secret spy safe havens. A spy could go to one of these safe houses to retire in peace without worrying about anyone settling old scores. Not only is this an intriguing and semi believable idea, Morrell milks all of the twists and turns that are possible when two spies that are mortal enemies become trapped in the one place where they are prevented from harming each other.<br />Last words: Brotherhood is not that convincing if you are hoping for a look at real tradecraft. However, when viewed among other spy thrillers this ranks very high with not only interesting and unique characters, but a really neat concept.<br /><br />More spy news and reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.spywrite.com">http://www.spywrite.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14092765132223608966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1441967266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16450134368097540484">4.5......This book was written in the early 80's and was set some time after the Vietnam war. It's a story of two men, orphaned at a young age and brought up by a man who trained them in a military system. They grew to love him as a father and after the war he trained them even more into being the elite of the elite in special forces. So it comes as a shock when he decides to kill them. <br/><br/>I really liked this book. It was a random one I pulled while at the library browsing. I'd never read David Mor</span>
  <span id="freeText16450134368097540484" style="display:none">4.5......This book was written in the early 80's and was set some time after the Vietnam war. It's a story of two men, orphaned at a young age and brought up by a man who trained them in a military system. They grew to love him as a father and after the war he trained them even more into being the elite of the elite in special forces. So it comes as a shock when he decides to kill them. <br /><br />I really liked this book. It was a random one I pulled while at the library browsing. I'd never read David Morrell but the title caught my eye and the synopsis sounded good. From the beginning this book was action packed. Very Jason Bourne-ish but with not as many resources. Because of its time setting it was kind of fun to watch them gain information through dictionaries, encyclopedias and fold out maps. <br /><br />I think this might be a series but it seemed like a stand alone book. Either way, I liked Morrell's style and will definitely look into reading more of his books. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/371140342?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer371140342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4708885524235501638"><b>Like all Morrell books, a good bit of action </b><br/><br/>Synopsis: <br/><br/><b>
  <i>Brotherhood of the Rose</i>
</b> is set in the Cold War era in the world of big time spies. Two orphans living in an orphanage, Saul and Chris, were singled out for education and training that led to them being paired together as super spies working for the CIA. Now, the man who trained them - the man they consider to be their father - has betrayed them. Saul and Chris avoid all sorts of troubles as they unravel an international plot against them</span>
  <span id="freeText4708885524235501638" style="display:none"><b>Like all Morrell books, a good bit of action </b><br /><br />Synopsis: <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Brotherhood of the Rose</i>
</b> is set in the Cold War era in the world of big time spies. Two orphans living in an orphanage, Saul and Chris, were singled out for education and training that led to them being paired together as super spies working for the CIA. Now, the man who trained them - the man they consider to be their father - has betrayed them. Saul and Chris avoid all sorts of troubles as they unravel an international plot against them and combat the international forces arrayed against them. <br /><br />My review: <br /><br />Like in all of Morrell's books, there is plenty of well-written action and interesting characters. Plenty of thought went into this world of conspiracy. The action is detailed, but not overly so. It is not Morrell's best work, but it is certainly worth the read.<br /><br />Read all of my reviews of David Morrell's books at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://dwdsreviews.blogspot.com/search/label/David%20Morrell">http://dwdsreviews.blogspot.com/searc...</a></span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1745597888573504337">I love this book so much I read it three times over the years. Two highly trained CIA operatives that were once orphans are betrayed by the only father they ever knew. They desperately attempt to discover the truth as operatives from every network in the world hunt them down with orders to kill. It's a fast-paced race against time with plenty of plot twists and suspense to keep you glued to your reading chair! It was also a pretty cool TV movie about 20 years ago with Peter Strauss, David Morse,</span>

Two highly trained CIA operatives that were once orphans are betrayed by the only father they ever knew. They desperately attempt to discover the truth as operatives from every network in the world hunt them down with orders to kill. It's a fast-paced race against time with plenty of plot twists and suspense to keep you glued to your reading chair! It was also a pretty cool TV movie about 20 years ago with Peter Strauss, David Morse, Connie Sellecca and Robert Mitchum as the main characters. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1323913950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16645847427134041446"><strong>Another excellent book by Morrell</strong><br/><br/>This book was a real pioneer in the genre of espionage thrillers. It's smart, fast-paced, and just a great introduction to the character of Saul, The character the even today I believe would make a great hero for the big screen. David Morrell has done an interesting thing in the way it's in pairs then a violence with secret religious orders. There is a strong sense of grace in this book for even men that have committed unforgivable crimes. It's deeper than your a</span>
  <span id="freeText16645847427134041446" style="display:none"><strong>Another excellent book by Morrell</strong><br /><br />This book was a real pioneer in the genre of espionage thrillers. It's smart, fast-paced, and just a great introduction to the character of Saul, The character the even today I believe would make a great hero for the big screen. David Morrell has done an interesting thing in the way it's in pairs then a violence with secret religious orders. There is a strong sense of grace in this book for even men that have committed unforgivable crimes. It's deeper than your average action story, giving you a lot to chew on beyond the story itself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16645847427134041446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73004232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13100391040622758589">Great action packed book! Don't let the prologue lose you. If your eyes start glazing over after a few paragraphs of the prologue, just skip to Book 1 (chapter 1). It's an easy read from there and a page turner. I actually read this book more than once. First time was in the early 90's and then I read it again about 15 years later. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zzhLUc64v7NzGoeHiNgEllQTQWeknfMA9PXBShFvt2tBLIWNM/og//OgbKfW3IoIWanO5LmxczcwIfAT//xuhg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZfH8erRXOTn2Mq0WXCRoQfW2kIEecpSRQoGBUpvFkoTr5TKmSRWmdXaIRjYCIObf+AwfAgNeFKaGVbALdVZLaQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/12535.David_Morrell">About David Morrell</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/12535.David_Morrell"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1218135781p3/12535.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/12535.David_Morrell">David Morrell
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,225
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3777587123318815466">David Morrell is a Canadian novelist from Kitchener, Ontario, who has been living in the United States for a number of years. He is best known for his debut 1972 novel <i>First Blood</i>, which would later become a successful film franchise starring Sylvester Stallone. More recently, he has been writing the <i>Captain America</i> comic books limited-series <i>The Chosen</i>.</span>

</div>
